class="main-article-content"><div class="ecmRichText" style="margin-bottom:0px"><section><h2 id="network-response-codes" class="test_h2 markdown-h2"><span>Network response codes</span><a class="icon icon--link hash-link" href="#network-response-codes" aria-label="Network response codes"><img src="https://www.paypalobjects.com/btdevdoc/bundles/4.3.24/_assets/anchor-PKYVW2VT.svg" alt="AnchorIcon"/></a></h2><span>
    In addition to the
    </span><a href="/braintree/docs/reference/response/transaction/ruby#processor_response_code"><span>processor response code</span></a><span>
    and text, some transaction objects include a
    </span><a href="/braintree/docs/reference/response/transaction/ruby#network_response_code"><span>network response code</span></a><span>
    and text. </span><p class="markdown-p"></p><span>These network response values are the raw responses that the card network may return, and
    when present they can provide additional detail about why a request was approved or declined.
    However, this information is supplemental to the processor response code. Consider the processor
    response code to be the source of truth. </span><p class="markdown-p"></p><span>Each card network has distinct response codes:</span><p class="markdown-p"></p><ul class="list list--disc"><li><a href="/braintree/docs/guides/pinless-debit/optimized-debit-routing/network-response-codes#card-network-accel"><span>Accel</span></a></li><li><a href="/braintree/docs/guides/pinless-debit/optimized-debit-routing/network-response-codes#card-network-nyce"><span>NYCE</span></a></li><li><a href="/braintree/docs/guides/pinless-debit/optimized-debit-routing/network-response-codes#card-network-pulse"><span>Pulse</span></a></li><li><a href="/braintree/docs/guides/pinless-debit/optimized-debit-routing/network-response-codes#card-network-star-star-access"><span>Star, Star Acces</span></a></li><li><a href="/braintree/docs/guides/pinless-debit/optimized-debit-routing/network-response-codes#card-network-Maestro"><span>Maestro</span></a></li></ul><style data-emotion="css Neue",Arial,sans-serif;font-size:0.875rem;line-height:1.125rem;font-weight:400;border-spacing:0;border-collapse:separate;text-align:start;width:100%;}@media screen and (max-width: >td,.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >th{border-bottom:0.0625rem solid #545d68;border-top:0.0625rem solid transparent;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >td{padding:0.75rem;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >thead>tr{background-color:#1e2023;white-space:nowrap;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >thead>tr >th{position:relative;color:#202020;font-family:PayPalOpen-Bold,"Helvetica Neue",Arial,sans-serif;font-size:0.875rem;line-height:1.125rem;font-weight:700;border-bottom:0.0625rem solid '&' : '') + key + "=" + btoa(queryParamters[key])); const endPoint = "https://www.paypal.com/myaccount/privacy/cookieprefs/cookies?" + queryString; xhr.open('GET', endPoint); xhr.withCredentials = true; xhr.onreadystatechange = function () { if (xhr.readyState > 3 && xhr.status === 200) { try { if (xhr?.response && xhr.response != "OK") { const invalidCookies = bodyPaddingBottom) { isPaddingBottomAdded = false; } } } } if (addListener) { adjustPaddingBottomEvent(); window.addEventListener('resize', adjustPaddingBottomEvent);  } else { var cookieBannerAcceptAll = document.getElementsByClassName("ccpaCookieBanner-acceptedAll"); if(cookieBannerAcceptAll && cookieBannerAcceptAll[0]){ window.removeEventListener('resize', adjustPaddingBottomEvent); adjustPaddingBottomEvent(); if (isPaddingBottomAdded && cookieBannerAcceptAll[0].style.paddingBottom === bannerPaddingBottom) { Network Response Codes\nslug: /docs/guides/pinless-debit/optimized-debit-routing/network-response-codes/\ncreateTime: '2025-04-02T02:05:19.338Z'\nupdateTime: '2025-04-02T02:05:19.390Z'\n---\n\n\n\n## Network response codes\n\nIn addition to the[processor response code](/braintree/docs/reference/response/transaction/ruby#processor_response_code)and text, some transaction objects include a[network response code](/braintree/docs/reference/response/transaction/ruby#network_response_code)and text.\n\nThese network response values are the raw responses that the card network may return, and when present they can provide additional detail about why a request was approved or declined. However, this information is supplemental to the processor response code. Consider the processor response code to be the source of truth.\n\nEach card network has distinct response codes:\n\n\n- [Accel](#card-network-accel)\n- [NYCE](#card-network-nyce)\n- [Pulse](#card-network-pulse)\n- [Star, Star Acces](#card-network-star-star-access)\n- [Maestro](#card-network-Maestro)\n\n| Card Network | Code | Text |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| Accel | 000 | Approved |\n| Accel | 001 | Approved with identification |\n| Accel | 002 | Approved for partial amount |\n| Accel | 003 | Approved (VIP) |\n| Accel | 100 | Do not honor (general denial) |\n| Accel | 101 | Expired card |\n| Accel | 102 | Suspected fraud |\n| Accel | 103 | Card acceptor contact acquirer |\n| Accel | 104 | Restricted card |\n| Accel | 105 | Card acceptor call acquirer's security department |\n| Accel | 106 | Allowable PIN tries exceeded |\n| Accel | 107 | Refer to card issuer |\n| Accel | 108 | Refer to card issuer's special condition |\n| Accel | 109 | Invalid merchant |\n| Accel | 110 | Invalid amount |\n| Accel | 111 | Invalid card number |\n| Accel | 112 | PIN data required |\n| Accel | 113 | Unacceptable fee |\n| Accel | 114 | No account of type requested |\n| Accel | 115 | Requested function not supported (invalid transaction) |\n| Accel | 116 | Insufficient funds |\n| Accel | 117 | Incorrect PIN |\n| Accel | 118 | No card record |\n| Accel | 119 | Transaction not permitted to cardholder |\n| Accel | 120 | Transaction not permitted to terminal |\n| Accel | 121 | Exceeds withdrawal amount limits |\n| Accel | 122 | Security violation |\n| Accel | 123 | Exceeds withdrawal limit frequency |\n| Accel | 124 | Violation of law |\n| Accel | 126 | Invalid PIN block |\n| Accel | 127 | PIN length error |\n| Accel | 128 | PIN key synchronization error |\n| Accel | 129 | Suspected counterfeit card |\n| Accel | 130 | Transaction failed OFAC check |\n| Accel | 131 | Check not acceptable |\n| Accel | 180 | Limit exceeded due to cash back amount |\n| Accel | 181 | Enter lesser amount |\n| Accel | 182 | Institution not supported by switch |\n| Accel | 183 | Balances not available for inquiry |\n| Accel | 184 | Resubmission in violation of network rules |\n| Accel | 185 | Stop Payment on check (shared branch only) |\n| Accel | 200 | Do not honor |\n| Accel | 201 | Expired card-Denial advice |\n| Accel | 202 | Suspected fraud |\n| Accel | 203 | Card acceptor contact acquirer |\n| Accel | 204 | Restricted card |\n| Accel | 205 | Card acceptor call acquirer's security department |\n| Accel | 206 | Allowable PIN tries exceeded |\n| Accel | 207 | Special conditions |\n| Accel | 208 | Lost card |\n| Accel | 209 | Stolen card |\n| Accel | 210 | Suspected counterfeit card |\n| Accel | 211 | Invalid card number |\n| Accel | 214 | No account of delay) |\n| NYCE | 10 | Partial Approval |\n| NYCE | 12 | Invalid transaction |\n| NYCE | 13 | Invalid amount |\n| NYCE | 14 | Invalid card number (no such number) |\n| NYCE | 15 | Cardholder not on file |\n| NYCE | 24 | File update not supported by receiver (only in 03xx) |\n| NYCE | 25 | Unable to locate record on file (only in 03xx) |\n| NYCE | 26 | Duplicate file update record, no action
